#10 7.175 Reporting Issues
#10 7.175 ================
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 Issues can be reported in the master issue tracker at:
#10 7.175 https://github.com/deadsnakes/issues/issues
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
#10 7.175 ====================================
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
#10 7.175 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
#10 7.175 - Note: Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 Why some packages aren't built:
#10 7.175 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
#10 7.175 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 Packages
#10 7.175 ========
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
#10 7.175 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
#10 7.175 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
#10 7.175 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
#10 7.175 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
#10 7.175 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 Third-Party Python Modules
#10 7.175 ==========================
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
#10 7.175 
#10 7.175 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
#10 7.175 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
#10 7.175

#10 7.175 =======
#10 7.175 The package sources are available at:
#10 7.175 https://github.com/deadsnakes/
